Methods 12, 59–60 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8#ref-CR128" id="ref-link-section-d52717e4251">128</a></sup> against a protein data set of 11 cyanobacterial genomes. This resulted in 30,312 <i>Azolla</i> genome contigs hitting 8,779 different cyanobacterial proteins that were used as a query in a tBLASTn<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d52717e4259">73</a></sup> against the <i>Azolla</i> genome; 340 <i>Azolla</i> contigs had reciprocal hits. To investigate whether these represent possible <i>Nostoc</i>-to-<i>Azolla</i> transfers or just examples of plastid-to-nucleus transfers, we used the 340 <i>Azolla</i> contigs for another BLASTx against the cyanobacteria and extracted all 51,743 BLASTx<i>-</i>aligned <i>Azolla</i> sequences. These highly redundant protein sequences were used for a DIAMOND BLASTp against the non-redundant database of NCBI. Almost all of the sequences had streptophyte proteins as the top hit, and when not, phylogenetic analysis clearly placed them within streptophytes.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec28">Phylogeny of SHC</h3><p>Homologues of SHC and oxidosqualene cyclase were obtained by searching against Phytozome<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 95" title="Goodstein, D. M. et al. Phytozome: a comparative platform for green plant genomics. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, D1178–D1186 (2012)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d52717e4293">95</a></sup>, 1KP transcriptomes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Matasci, N. et al. Data access for the 1,000 Plants (1KP) project. GigaScience 3, 1–10 (2014)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d52717e4297">32</a></sup> and the NCBI Genbank non-redundant protein database. Protein alignment was done in MUSCLE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 99" title="Edgar, R. C. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, 1792–1797 (2004)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d52717e4301">99</a></sup>. We used IQ-TREE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 116" title="Nguyen, L.-T., Schmidt, H. A., von Haeseler, A. &amp; Minh, B. Q. IQ-TREE: a fast and effective stochastic algorithm for estimating maximum-likelihood phylogenies. Mol. Biol. Evol. 32, 268–274 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8#ref-CR116" id="ref-link-section-d52717e4305">116</a></sup> to find the best-fitting amino acid substitution model and infer the phylogeny using maximum likelihood. Bootstrap support was assessed with 1,000 pseudoreplicates. To test whether the monophyly of fern, lycophyte, moss and liverwort SHC could be rejected, we conducted a Swofford–Olsen–Waddell–Hillis test using SOWHAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Church, S. H., Ryan, J. F. &amp; Dunn, C. W. Automation and evaluation of the SOWH test with SOWHAT. Syst. Biol. 64, 1048–1058 (2015)." href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d52717e4309">48</a></sup>. We compared the best maximum likelihood topology against the topology with all land plant SHC constrained to be monophyletic. SOWHAT was run with 1,000 replicates.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec29">Detection of SHC-synthesized triterpenes</h3><p>Freeze-dried <i>S.</i> <i>cucullata</i> biomass was Soxhlet extracted in a 9:1 DCM:MeOH mixture for 24 h. The total lipid extracts obtained were dried over Na<sub>2</sub>SO<sub>4</sub> followed by evaporation of the solvent by a gentle stream of N<sub>2</sub>. Aliquots of the total lipid extracts were methylated with diazomethane to convert the acid groups into corresponding methyl esters, purified over a SiO<sub>2</sub> column and silylated using bis(trimethylsilyl)trifluoracetamide (BSTFA) in pyridine at 60 °C for 20 min to convert the hydroxy groups into the corresponding trimethylsilyl ethers. The total lipid extracts were on-column injected on a Thermo Trace GC Ultra Trace DSQ gas chromatography mass spectrometry (GC–MS) onto a CP-sil 5CB-fused silica column (30 m × 0.32 mm internal diameter, film thickness: 0.10 μm). The GC–MS was operated at a constant flow of 1.0 ml min<sup>−1</sup>. The GC oven was programmed starting at 70 °C to rise to 130 °C at a rate of 20 °C per min and then to 320 °C at a rate of 4 °C per min, followed by an isothermal hold for 20 min.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec30">Reporting Summary</h3><p>Further information on experimental design is available in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8#MOESM2">Nature Research Reporting Summary</a> linked to this article.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec31">Data availability</h3><p>The genome assemblies and annotations can be found at <a href="http://www.fernbase.org">www.fernbase.org</a>. The raw genomic and transcriptomic reads generated in this study were deposited in the NCBI SRA under the BioProject <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=PRJNA430527">PRJNA430527</a> and <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra?term=PRJNA430459">PRJNA430459</a>. The sequence alignments and tree files can be found in the <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8#MOESM1">Supplementary Data</a>.</p></div></div></section>

                </p></li><li class="c-article-references__item js-c-reading-companion-references-item" itemprop="citation" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle"><meta itemprop="author" content="EB.     <a data-track="click" data-track-action="outbound reference" data-track-label="link" aria-label="Search for reference 6 on Google Scholar" href="http://scholar.google.com/scholar_lookup?&amp;title=Evolutionary%20genomics%20of%20ferns%20and%20lycophytes&amp;journal=Adv.%20Bot.%20Res.&amp;volume=78&amp;pages=215-254&amp;publication_year=2016&amp;author=Sessa%2CEB&amp;author=Der%2CJP">
                    Google Scholar</a> 
                </p></li><li class="c-article-references__item js-c-reading-companion-references-item" itemprop="citation" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle"><meta itemprop="author" content="H. F.-W.L., J.P.D., H.S., G.K.-S.W. and K.M.P. coordinated the project. P.B., Y.-M.H., Y.K. and H.S. provided plant materials. F.-W.L. and L.-Y.K. performed flow cytometry to estimate genome sizes. F.-W.L., S.C., B.H., X.L., Y.S., H.W. and X.X. undertook the sequencing activities. N.K. and A.B. assembled the <i>Azolla</i> genome. F.-W.L. and S.C. assembled the <i>Salvinia</i> genome. F.-W.L., S.C., X.L., Y.S., H.W. and X.X. assembled and annotated the symbiotic cyanobacteria genomes. M.S. and J.P.D. annotated the nuclear genomes. F.-W.L., T.R. and P.G.W. assembled and annotated the plastid genomes. M.S., S.A. and J.P.D. characterized the repeat content. L.C.-P., M.S., I.S., E.W., C.d., S.M., R.M., S.A.R., P.R.T., Y.V.d.P., P.K.I.W. and J.P.D. performed the gene functional annotation. L.C.-P., E.W., C.d., S.M., P.R.T. and Y.V.d.P. conducted the gene family classification. Z.L. and M.S.B. performed the MAPS analyses. L.C.-P., S.M. and Y.V.d.P. carried out the synteny analyses. S.C., I.S., X.L., R.M., Y.S., H.W. and X.X. characterized the PPR gene family and RNA editing. J.d.V. and S.G. examined the cyanobiont-to-<i>Azolla</i> HGT. P.-M.D. characterized the common symbiosis genes. F.-W.L., S.C., A.E., X.L., Y.S., H.W. and X.X. carried out the RNA-seq analyses. F.-W.L. and P.B. conducted the phylogenetic analyses. P.B. and K.G.J.N. carried out the triterpene detection. P.S.H. and L.A.M. constructed FernBase. F.-W.L., P.B., L.C.-P., S.C., A.E., M.S., J.d.V., P.-M.D., N.K., L.-Y.K., Z.L., I.S., E.W., J.P.D., H.S., G.K.-S.W. and K.M.P. contributed to writing the manuscript. F.-W.L. and K.M.P. organized the manuscript.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding author</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
                <a id="corresp-c1" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41477-018-0188-8/email/correspondent/c1/new">Fay-Wei Li</a>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="ethics" data-title="Ethics declarations"><div class="c-article-section" id="ethics-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="ethics">Ethics declarations</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="ethics-content">
